         <h3 id="ruma" style="position:relative"><a href="#ruma" aria-label="ruma permalink" class="anchor before">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>Ruma</h3>
         <p><a href="https://www.ruma.io/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">Ruma</a> is a set of Rust library crates around Matrix</p>
         <p><a href="https://matrix.to/#/@jplatte:flipdot.org" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">jplatte</a> offered:</p>
         <blockquote>
          <p>We've been quiet in the past weeks, but certainly not due to lack of activity! So many awesome things have happened, I don't even know where to start. I guess I'll go chronologically:</p>
          <p><strong>We published so many new crate releases.</strong> Most of our crates didn't see non-alpha releases for almost a year and now we've finally reset that counter! Now you can depend on <code class="language-text">ruma 0.1</code> and get bug fixes and new functionality through <code class="language-text">cargo update</code> without having to worry about breaking changes. Huge thanks to <a href="https://github.com/zecakeh" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">@zecakeh</a> for automating our release process, without that this would have taken so much longer.</p>
          <p><strong>We got initial spaces support!</strong> I'm super excited that we're now enabling client authors to take spaces into account, even if "taking into account" will initially just mean filtering out space rooms from their room lists. Code-wise, this was actually a <a href="https://github.com/ruma/ruma/pull/585" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">relatively small change</a>, with ruma-client-api receiving support for room types and ruma-events receiving support for the event types <code class="language-text">m.space.child</code> and <code class="language-text">m.space.parent</code>.</p>
          <p><strong>We're swapping out ruma-signatures' crypto library.</strong> Since <code class="language-text">ring</code>, which is what we've been using so far, doesn't currently support cross-compilation to WASM, there's long been some interest to exchange it for something else for webbrowser homeserver experiments. A viable alternative library was identified a while ago and now <a href="https://github.com/ShadowJonathan" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">@ShadowJonathan</a> has taken on the task of <a href="https://github.com/ruma/ruma/pull/589" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">implementing the switch</a>.</p>
          <p>In addition to unblocking the WASM usecase, this work <a href="https://github.com/briansmith/ring/issues/1299" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">revealed a bug in <code class="language-text">ring</code></a>, which generated invalid PKCS#8 documents. We are pretty confident that once the switch away from <code class="language-text">ring</code> (including a small compatibility shim to convert the invalid documents), a certain class of signature verification failures that Conduit has been getting will be fixed.</p>
          <p><strong>We're taking part in GSoC again.</strong> As you might have seen in the <a href="https://matrix.org/blog/2021/05/20/google-summer-of-code-2021" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">earlier blog post</a>, two students are working on Ruma as part of GSoC this year: <a href="https://github.com/Frinksy" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">@Frinksy</a> (for the first time) and <a href="https://github.com/DevinR528" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">@DevinR528</a> (for the second time).</p>
          <p><strong>Apart from that,</strong></p>
          <ul>
           <li><p><a href="https://github.com/132ikl" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">@132ikl</a> fixed <a href="https://github.com/ruma/ruma/pull/529" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">a bug with unsetting avatar URLs</a></p></li>
           <li><p><a href="https://github.com/abhikjain360" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">@abhikjain360</a> added <a href="https://github.com/ruma/ruma/pull/515" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">email validation endpoints to ruma-identity-service-api</a></p></li>
           <li><p><a href="https://github.com/132ikl" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">@132ikl</a> fixed <a href="https://github.com/ruma/ruma/pull/533" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">a small bug in our release automation</a></p></li>
           <li><p><a href="https://github.com/Frinksy" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">@Frinksy</a> added <a href="https://github.com/ruma/ruma/pull/534" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">helpers to construct the fallback for rich replies</a></p></li>
           <li><p><a href="https://github.com/132ikl" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">@132ikl</a> improved <a href="https://github.com/ruma/ruma/pull/536" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">event relation support for encrypted events</a></p></li>
           <li><p><a href="https://github.com/jplatte" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">@jplatte</a> (that's me) made <a href="https://github.com/ruma/ruma/pull/539" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">ruma-client independent of the underlying HTTP client library</a></p></li>
           <li><p><a href="https://github.com/abhikjain360" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">@abhikjain360</a> added <a href="https://github.com/ruma/ruma/pull/540" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">phone number validation endpoints to ruma-identity-service-api</a></p></li>
           <li><p><a href="https://github.com/gnieto" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">@gnieto</a> fixed <a href="https://github.com/ruma/ruma/pull/542" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">a small serialization bug in ruma-federation-api</a></p></li>
           <li><p><a href="https://github.com/DevinR528" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">@DevinR528</a> cleaned up <a href="https://github.com/ruma/ruma/pull/544" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">our crate manifest files</a></p></li>
           <li><p><a href="https://github.com/zecakeh" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">@zecakeh</a> added <a href="https://github.com/ruma/ruma/pull/546" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">a <code class="language-text">TagName</code> type for <code class="language-text">m.tag</code> events</a> (+ <a href="https://github.com/ruma/ruma/pull/549" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">followup API improvement</a>)</p></li>
           <li><p><a href="https://github.com/DevinR528" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">@DevinR528</a> enabled <a href="https://github.com/ruma/ruma/pull/553" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">a set of lints across the entire project</a></p></li>

         <h3 id="matrix-docker-ansible-deploy" style="position:relative"><a href="#matrix-docker-ansible-deploy" aria-label="matrix docker ansible deploy permalink" class="anchor before">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>matrix-docker-ansible-deploy</h3>
         <p>This <a href="https://github.com/spantaleev/matrix-docker-ansible-deploy" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">Ansible playbook</a> is meant to easily let you run your own Matrix homeserver.</p>
         <p><a href="https://matrix.to/#/@slavi:devture.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">Slavi</a> told us:</p>
         <blockquote>
          <p>Thanks to <a href="https://github.com/aaronraimist" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">Aaron Raimist</a>, <a href="https://github.com/spantaleev/matrix-docker-ansible-deploy" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">matrix-docker-ansible-deploy</a> now supports <a href="https://github.com/vector-im/hydrogen-web" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">Hydrogen</a> - a new lightweight matrix client with legacy and mobile browser support.</p>
          <p>By default, we still install Element, as Hydrogen is still not fully-featured. Still, people who'd like to try Hydrogen out can now install it via the playbook.</p>
          <p>Additional details are available in <a href="https://github.com/spantaleev/matrix-docker-ansible-deploy/blob/master/docs/configuring-playbook-client-hydrogen.md" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">Setting up Hydrogen</a>.</p>
         </blockquote>
         <p>Also...</p>
         <blockquote>
          <p>Thanks to <a href="https://github.com/hifi" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">Toni Spets (hifi)</a>, <a href="https://github.com/spantaleev/matrix-docker-ansible-deploy" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">matrix-docker-ansible-deploy</a> now supports bridging to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internet_Relay_Chat" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">IRC</a> using yet another bridge (besides <a href="https://github.com/matrix-org/matrix-appservice-irc" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">matrix-appservice-irc</a>), called <a href="https://github.com/hifi/heisenbridge" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">Heisenbridge</a>.</p>
          <p>To get started, see our <a href="https://github.com/spantaleev/matrix-docker-ansible-deploy/blob/master/docs/configuring-playbook-bridge-heisenbridge.md" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">Setting up Heisenbridge bouncer-style IRC bridging</a> documentation.</p>
         </blockquote>

         <h3 id="community---space-bot" style="position:relative"><a href="#community---space-bot" aria-label="community   space bot permalink" class="anchor before">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>Community -&gt; Space Bot</h3>
         <p><a href="https://github.com/turt2live" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">TravisR</a> said:</p>
         <blockquote>
          <p>If you're trying out all those cool <a href="https://matrix.org/blog/2021/05/17/the-matrix-space-beta" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">Spaces</a> (<a href="https://element.io/blog/spaces-the-next-frontier/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">Element Blog</a>) and have some old Communities/Groups hanging around, I have the bot for you.</p>
          <p><a href="https://t2bot.io/spacebot/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">spacebot</a> makes quick work of the conversion by translating as much as possible to the Space structure. Simply DM the bot and say <code class="language-text">!convert +group:example.org</code> and it'll go off and make your Space.</p>
          <p>The bot doesn't invite everyone from your Community to your Space, giving you a chance to configure the Space further before advertising it within your rooms.</p>
          <p>The source can be found on <a href="https://github.com/t2bot/groups-to-space-bot" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">GitHub</a> if you feel like running your own or seeing how simple it is under the hood. <a href="https://matrix.to/#/#spacebot:t2bot.io" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">#spacebot:t2bot.io</a> is a great place to get help if you're having problems getting it going, and <a href="https://matrix.to/#/#help:t2bot.io" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">#help:t2bot.io</a> would be glad to assist you if the t2bot.io deployment doesn't do the right thing.</p>
          <p>P.S.: Spaces are currently considered Beta in Element, so they might not be perfect just yet. <a href="https://matrix.to/#/#spaces:riot.ovh" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">#spaces:riot.ovh</a> is the room to join if you have questions about Spaces.</p>
         </blockquote>

           </svg></a>raspberry-noaa-v2 matrix support</h3>
         <p><a href="https://matrix.to/#/@cadair:cadair.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">Cadair</a> said:</p>
         <blockquote>
          <p>A little bit different, but matrix related, this week I <a href="https://github.com/jekhokie/raspberry-noaa-v2/blob/master/docs/matrix_push.md" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">added Matrix push</a> support to the <a href="https://github.com/jekhokie/raspberry-noaa-v2/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">raspberry-noaa-v2</a> project. This is a project which runs on a raspberry pi to automate receiving, decoding and post processing of images over radio from weather satellites. It's easy to build a cheap ground station for this with little more than a USB SDR dongle and a metal coat hanger. If you want to see the pictures I am decoding you can join <a href="https://matrix.to/#/#weather:cadair.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">#weather:cadair.com</a>.</p>
         </blockquote>
         <p>Cadair, living in the north of England, will only see this symbol unfortunately ??</p>
         <h3 id="server_stats-voyager-project" style="position:relative"><a href="#server_stats-voyager-project" aria-label="server_stats voyager project permalink" class="anchor before">

            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>Server_Stats Voyager Project</h3>
         <p><a href="https://matrix.to/#/@mtrnord:nordgedanken.dev" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">MTRNord</a> announced:</p>
         <blockquote>
          <p>The Project now has a proper webpage at <a href="https://serverstats.nordgedanken.dev/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">https://serverstats.nordgedanken.dev/</a> !</p>
          <h4 id="newly-added-features-are" style="position:relative"><a href="#newly-added-features-are" aria-label="newly added features are permalink" class="anchor before">
            <svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
             <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
            </svg></a>Newly added Features are:</h4>
          <ul>
           <li><p>A List of all the rooms that are found</p></li>
           <li><p>A list to find the links (either outgoing or incoming) for a room. So a 1 level deep view into the graph as a table.</p></li>
           <li><p>An FAQ with some information about the project, known data issues and more</p></li>
           <li><p>A websocket at <code class="language-text">wss://serverstats.nordgedanken.dev/ws</code> that allows you to get the updates directly pushed as soon as a room lands in the db. Effectively the fastest way to get data updates.</p></li>
          </ul>
          <h4 id="planned-features-for-the-webpage" style="position:relative"><a href="#planned-features-for-the-webpage" aria-label="planned features for the webpage permalink" class="anchor before">
            <svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
             <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
            </svg></a>Planned features for the webpage</h4>
          <ul>
           <li><p>AR and VR Graphs</p></li>
           <li><p>A Space Finder that allows you to find the discovered spaces</p></li>
          </ul>
          <p>Be aware that this page is very new and therefor might have bugs. It also isn't yet mobile optimized.</p>
          <p>For questions, suggestions or fast updates check the #server_stats:nordgedanken.dev Room or for questions regarding issues with the bot in a specific room feel free to write a DM to <a href="https://matrix.to/#/@mtrnord:nordgedanken.dev" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">MTRNord</a> :)</p>
          <h4 id="possible-bug-that-needs-manual-fixing" style="position:relative"><a href="#possible-bug-that-needs-manual-fixing" aria-label="possible bug that needs manual fixing permalink" class="anchor before">
            <svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
             <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
            </svg></a>Possible Bug that needs manual fixing</h4>
          <p>Due to a bug with my homeserver or synapse it happens for some rooms that synapse generates a lot of join events (Lots of "server_stats bot made no change" messages). If you see this please write a message to <a href="https://matrix.to/#/@mtrnord:nordgedanken.dev" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">MTRNord</a> so I can manually prevent my bot from trying to join the room over and over again as I cannot easily detect this kind of issue before joining. </p>
          <p>The issue can be followed at <a href="https://github.com/matrix-org/synapse/issues/10021" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">https://github.com/matrix-org/synapse/issues/10021</a></p>
         </blockquote>

        <h1 class="Article__Title-ejf3ys-0 kUhord"><a href="/blog/2021/05/20/google-summer-of-code-2021">Google Summer of Code 2021</a></h1>
        <div class="Subline-z3aujq-0 fCCPho">
         2021-05-20<!-- --> —&nbsp;<a href="/blog/category/gsoc">GSOC</a> —&nbsp;<!-- -->Ben Parsons
        </div>
        <div class="Article__PostContent-ejf3ys-1 dltekG">
         <p><a href="https://summerofcode.withgoogle.com" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">Google Summer of Code 2021</a> participants have been announced! This year <a href="https://summerofcode.withgoogle.com/organizations/6691635666092032/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">Matrix has been assigned <em>seven</em> students</a>.</p>
         <h2 id="projects" style="position:relative"><a href="#projects" aria-label="projects permalink" class="anchor before">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>Projects</h2>
         <h3 id="r-midhun-suresh-right-sidebar-for-hydrogen-client" style="position:relative"><a href="#r-midhun-suresh-right-sidebar-for-hydrogen-client" aria-label="r midhun suresh right sidebar for hydrogen client permalink" class="anchor before">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>R Midhun Suresh: <em>Right Sidebar for Hydrogen client</em></h3>
         <blockquote>
          <p>R Midhun Suresh from the Mar Baselios College of Engineering &amp; Technology in Trivandrum, India will be working on Hydrogen this summer, mentored by Bruno Windels. He will be working on adding a right panel to the room view, including a member list and room information. He will be blogging at <a href="https://midhunsureshr.github.io" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">https://midhunsureshr.github.io</a> throughout the project.</p>
         </blockquote>
         <h3 id="devin-ragotzy-rumas-automated-checks" style="position:relative"><a href="#devin-ragotzy-rumas-automated-checks" aria-label="devin ragotzy rumas automated checks permalink" class="anchor before">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>Devin Ragotzy: <em>Ruma's Automated Checks</em></h3>
         <blockquote>
          <p>My name is Devin Ragotzy. I am a student at Western Michigan University in Kalamazoo, Michigan, studying computer science. I was lucky enough to work last summer on Ruma and have continued to contribute to the project. I was accepted to work on Ruma's automated checks project, mentored by Isaiah Inuwa, Jonas Platte, Timo Kösters. The goal of the project is to create a linter capable of enforcing Ruma-specific style and practices. I hope to get this tool to a working state by the end of this summers GSoC!</p>
         </blockquote>
         <h3 id="abhinav-krishna-c-k-first-class-email-bridge" style="position:relative"><a href="#abhinav-krishna-c-k-first-class-email-bridge" aria-label="abhinav krishna c k first class email bridge permalink" class="anchor before">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>Abhinav Krishna C K: <em>First-Class Email Bridge</em></h3>
         <blockquote>
          <p>Abhinav Krishna C K from NSS College of Engineering in Palakkad, India will be working on Building First-Class email bridge for Matrix this summer mentored by Half-Shot and tulir. This will enable Matrix to be connected with Email by translating incoming SMTP traffic to Matrix messages, and then bridging Matrix messages back into emails.</p>
         </blockquote>
         <h3 id="frinksy-extend-rumas-api-coverage" style="position:relative"><a href="#frinksy-extend-rumas-api-coverage" aria-label="frinksy extend rumas api coverage permalink" class="anchor before">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>Frinksy: <em>Extend Ruma's API coverage</em></h3>
         <blockquote>
          <p>My name is Adam Blanchet, and I am a student from the University of York in the UK.<br> <!-- -->I am happy to say that I have quite a few mentors: Isaiah Inuwa, Jonas Platte, Timo Kösters and Nico from Nheko.<br> <!-- -->My project is to extend Ruma's API coverage. I'll be doing a few things: finishing coverage of the Identity Service API, adding the "knock" feature to Ruma and finishing the implementation of QR code verification. If time allows it I will also work on implementing other MSCs or features such as "Event notification attributes and actions". I hope that my work will help enable other Rust-based Matrix projects, such as Conduit and Fractal, to implement more features.</p>
         </blockquote>
         <p>Timo added:</p>
         <blockquote>
          <p>Hello, I am Timo Kösters. I study Computer Science in Germany and spend most of the remaining time developing Conduit, a Matrix homeserver built on top of Ruma. I use Ruma all the time and will be mentoring Adam Blanchet to make it even better.</p>
         </blockquote>
         <h3 id="vladyslav-hnatiuk-pyquotient" style="position:relative"><a href="#vladyslav-hnatiuk-pyquotient" aria-label="vladyslav hnatiuk pyquotient permalink" class="anchor before">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>Vladyslav Hnatiuk: <em>PyQuotient</em></h3>
         <blockquote>
          <p>My name is Vladyslav Hnatiuk, I'm a student of Vienna University of Technology and my project is PyQuotient.<br> <!-- -->The aim is to simplify creating of a Matrix Qt-based clients in Python by providing Qt-based SDK and avoid writing a large part of functionality manually. And to not reinvent the wheel PyQuotient will be bindings for the existing library libQuotient that provides SDK for Matrix for C++ applications. I'll be mentored by kitsune, the author of libQuotient and also libQuotient-based Matrix IM client Quaternion. I hope PyQuotient will facilitate the development of Matrix clients in Python with Qt, and it will be a small contribution to the promotion of Matrix, especially in Python world.</p>
         </blockquote>
         <p>kitsune added:</p>
         <blockquote>
          <p>If this experience proves to be successful, there’s a good chance Quaternion will eventually switch to Python.</p>
         </blockquote>
         <h3 id="callum-brown-token-authenticated-registration" style="position:relative"><a href="#callum-brown-token-authenticated-registration" aria-label="callum brown token authenticated registration permalink" class="anchor before">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>Callum Brown: <em>Token Authenticated Registration</em></h3>
         <blockquote>
          <p>Hi there, I'm Callum, a Londoner who'll be starting a physics degree in September. For GSoC I'll be working on adding Token Authenticated Registration to Matrix. This will allow homeserver admins to restrict who can sign-up by requiring a token to be submitted during registration. I run a small homeserver for friends and family, but don't have the resources to make registration public, so I have wanted this feature integrated into Matrix servers and clients for quite a while! I'll be working with Nico, anoa, and red_sky to write an MSC, implement the server side in Synapse, and the client side in Nheko. Thanks to the mentors and Matrix.org for the opportunity to work on this!</p>
         </blockquote>
         <p>You can follow along with this project's progress throughout the program at <a href="https://calcuode.com/matrix-gsoc/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">https://calcuode.com/matrix-gsoc/</a>.</p>
         <p>Nico, mentor added:</p>
         <blockquote>
          <p>Nico here, one of the Mentors. Personally I am super excited about this project! I have been using Matrix for a while now and I think Nheko is pretty good by now. But there is still a barrier, if I want my friends and family to use Matrix: They can't easily sign up! I have tried creating them accounts and telling them to change their passwords, having a dedicated registration page or just telling them to just use a different server, but nothing of that made me happy and it added friction to the already hard process of getting someone to try a new messenger! As such I am super excited for this, because it will make signing up your friends and family to your personal instance, without it having to be public, sooooo much simpler!</p>
         </blockquote>
         <h3 id="jaiwanth-exporting-conversations-from-element" style="position:relative"><a href="#jaiwanth-exporting-conversations-from-element" aria-label="jaiwanth exporting conversations from element permalink" class="anchor before">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>Jaiwanth: <em>Exporting Conversations From Element</em></h3>
         <blockquote>
          <p>Jaiwanth Vemula from the IIT Kharagpur University in India will be working on Exporting Conversations in Element this summer, mentored by Michael (t3chguy). This work will enable users to easily export their conversations for archival or sharing, this is a feature which has been missed in Element for a very long time!</p>
         </blockquote>
         <h2 id="fractal" style="position:relative"><a href="#fractal" aria-label="fractal permalink" class="anchor before">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>
           </svg></a>Fractal</h2>
         <p>There are also <a href="https://summerofcode.withgoogle.com/organizations/5276176043474944/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">two projects under the GNOME organisation</a> with students working on Fractal, a Matrix client for GNOME.</p>
         <ul>
          <li>Alejandro Domínguez: <em>Fractal: Multi account support</em></li>
          <li>Kai A. Hiller: <em>Fractal NEXT</em></li>
         </ul>
         <h2 id="students-become-mentors" style="position:relative"><a href="#students-become-mentors" aria-label="students become mentors permalink" class="anchor before">
           <svg aria-hidden="true" focusable="false" height="16" version="1.1" viewbox="0 0 16 16" width="16">
            <path fill-rule="evenodd" d="M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z"></path>

         <p>I asked: <em>how many of those who are mentors this year have ever been GSOC students?</em> The answer is that this year four of the mentors were once GSoC students themselves!</p>

         </ul>

       <div class="mxcontent__main__post">
        <h1 class="Article__Title-ejf3ys-0 kUhord"><a href="/blog/2021/05/19/how-the-u-ks-online-safety-bill-threatens-matrix">How the UK's Online Safety Bill threatens Matrix</a></h1>
        <div class="Subline-z3aujq-0 fCCPho">
         2021-05-19<!-- --> —&nbsp;<a href="/blog/category/tech">Tech</a>, <a href="/blog/category/general">General</a> —&nbsp;<!-- -->Denise Almeida
        </div>
        <div class="Article__PostContent-ejf3ys-1 dltekG">
         <p>Last week the UK government published a <a href="https://www.gov.uk/government/publications/draft-online-safety-bill" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">draft of the proposed Online Safety Bill,</a> after having initially introduced <a href="https://www.gov.uk/government/consultations/online-harms-white-paper/public-feedback/online-harms-white-paper-initial-consultation-response" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">formal proposals for said bill in early 2020</a>. With this post we aim to shed some light on its potential impacts and explain why we think that this bill - despite having great intentions - may actually be setting a dangerous precedent when it comes to our rights to privacy, freedom of expression and self determination.</p>
         <p>The proposed bill aims to provide a legal framework to address illegal and harmful content online. This focus on “not illegal, but harmful” content is at the centre of our concerns - it puts responsibility on organisations themselves to arbitrarily decide what might be harmful, without any legal backing. The bill itself does not actually provide a definition of harmful, instead relying on service providers to assess and decide on this. This requirement to identify what is “likely to be harmful” applies to all users, children and adults. Our question here is - would you trust a service provider to decide what might be harmful to you and your children, with zero input from you as a user?</p>
         <p>Additionally, the bill incentivises the use of privacy-invasive age verification processes which come with their own set of problems. This complete disregard of people’s right to privacy is a reflection of the privileged perspectives of those in charge of the drafting of this bill, which fails to acknowledge how <em>actually</em> harmful it would be for certain groups of the population to have their real life identity associated with their online identity.</p>
         <p>Our view of the world, and of the internet, is largely different from the one presented by this bill. Now, this categorically does not mean we don’t care about online safety (it is quite literally our bread and butter) - we just fundamentally disagree with the approach taken.</p>
         <p>Whilst we sympathise with the government’s desire to show action in this space and to do something about children’s safety (everyone’s safety really), we cannot possibly agree with the methods.</p>
         <p>Back in October of 2020 we presented <a href="https://matrix.org/blog/2020/10/19/combating-abuse-in-matrix-without-backdoors" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">our proposed approach to online safety</a> - ironically also in response to a government proposal, albeit about encryption backdoors. In it, we briefly discussed the dangers of absolute determinations of morality from a single cultural perspective:</p>
         <blockquote>
          <a href="https://matrix.org/blog/2020/10/19/combating-abuse-in-matrix-without-backdoors">As uncomfortable as it may be, one man’s terrorist is another man’s freedom fighter, and different jurisdictions have different laws - and it’s not up to the Matrix.org Foundation to play God and adjudicate.</a>
         </blockquote>
         <p>We now find ourselves reading a piece of legislation that essentially demands these determinations from tech companies. The beauty of the human experience lies with its diversity and when we force technology companies to make calls about what is right or wrong - or what is “likely to have adverse psychological or physical impacts” on children - we end up in a dangerous place of centralising and regulating relative morals. Worst of all, when the consequence of getting it wrong is criminal liability for senior managers what do we think will happen?</p>
         <p>Regardless of how omnipresent it is in our daily lives, technology is still not a solution for human problems. Forcing organisations to be judge and jury of human morals for the sake of “free speech” will, ironically, have severe consequences on free speech, as risk profiles will change for fear of liability.</p>
         <p>Forcing a “duty of care” responsibility on organisations which operate online will not only drown small and medium sized companies in administrative tasks and costs, it will further accentuate the existing monopolies by Big Tech. Plainly, Big Tech can afford the regulatory burden - small start-ups can’t. Future creators will have their wings clipped from the offset and we might just miss out on new ideas and projects for fear of legal repercussions. This is a threat to the technology sector, particularly those building on emerging technologies like Matrix. In some ways, it is a threat to democracy and some of the freedoms this bill claims to protect.</p>
         <p>These are, quite frankly, steps towards an authoritarian dystopia. If Trust &amp; Safety managers start censoring something as natural as a nipple on the off chance it might cause “adverse psychological impacts” on children, whose freedom of expression are we actually protecting here?</p>
         <p>More specifically on the issue of content moderation: the <a href="https://assets.publishing.service.gov.uk/government/uploads/system/uploads/attachment_data/file/985283/Draft_Online_Safety_Bill_-_Impact_Assessment_Web_Accessible.pdf" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">impact assessment provided by the government alongside this bill</a> predicts that the additional costs for companies directly related to the bill will be in the billions, over the course of 10 years. The cost for the government? £400k, in every proposed policy option. Our question is - why are these responsibilities being placed on tech companies, when evidently this is a societal problem?</p>
         <p>We are not saying it is up to the government to single-handedly end the existence of Child Sexual Abuse and Exploitation (CSAE) or extremist content online. What we are saying is that it takes more than content filtering, risk assessments and (faulty) age verification processes for it to end. More funding for tech literacy organisations and schools, to give children (and parents) the tools to stay safe is the first thing that comes to mind. Further investment in law enforcement cyber units and the judicial system, improving tech companies’ routes for abuse reporting and allowing the actual judges to do the judging seems pretty sensible too. What is absolutely egregious is the degradation of the digital rights of the majority, due to the wrongdoings of a few.</p>
         <p>Our goal with this post is not to be dramatic or alarmist. However, we want to add our voices to the countless <a href="https://www.openrightsgroup.org/blog/online-abuse-why-management-liability-isnt-the-answer/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">digital rights campaigners</a>, individuals and organisations that have been raising the alarm since the early days of this bill. Just like with coercive control and abuse, the degradation of our rights does not happen all at once. It is a slippery slope that starts with something as (seemingly) innocuous as <a href="https://twitter.com/matthew_d_green/status/1392823038920564736" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener noreferrer">mandatory content scanning for CSAE content and ends with authoritarian surveillance infrastructure</a>. It is our duty to put a stop to this before it even begins.</p><small style="display:block;text-align:right">Twitter card image credit from <a href="https://film-grab.com/2010/10/04/brazil/#bwg644/39614">Brazil</a>, which feels all too familiar right now.</small>
        </div>
        <div class="Article__LineBreak-ejf3ys-2 kgzjyp"></div>
       </div>
